<p><b>Muammar Muhammad Abu Minyar al-Gaddafi</b><sup id="cite_ref-iccwarrant_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iccwarrant-7"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language" class="mw-redirect">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl" xml:lang="ar">معمر محمد أبو منيار القذافي</span>‎; <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/oʊ/ long 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="/./ syllable break">.</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɑr/ 'ar' in 'bard'">ɑr</span></span> <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ɑː/ 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'f' in 'find'">f</span><span title="/i/ 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <span class="unicode haudio" style="white-space:nowrap;"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/File:Ar-Muammar_al-Qaddafi.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;<a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/86/Ar-Muammar_al-Qaddafi.ogg" class="internal" title="Ar-Muammar al-Qaddafi.ogg">audio</a></span>&#160;<small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:Ar-Muammar_al-Qaddafi.ogg" title="File:Ar-Muammar al-Qaddafi.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span>; <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1942</span>&#160;– 20 October 2011), commonly known as <b>Colonel Gaddafi</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>b<span>]</span></a></sup> was a <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libyan</a> revolutionary and politician who governed Libya as its primary leader from 1969 to 2011. Taking power in a coup d'etat, he ruled as Revolutionary Chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Libyan_Arab_Republic" title="Libyan Arab Republic" class="mw-redirect">Libyan Arab Republic</a> from 1969 to 1977 and then as the "<a href="/wiki/Brotherly_Leader_and_Guide_of_the_Revolution" title="Brotherly Leader and Guide of the Revolution">Brotherly Leader</a>" of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Socialist_People%27s_Libyan_Arab_Jamahiriya" title="Great Socialist People's Libyan Arab Jamahiriya" class="mw-redirect">Great Socialist People's Libyan Arab Jamahiriya</a> from 1977 to 2011, when he was ousted in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Libyan_Civil_War" title="2011 Libyan Civil War" class="mw-redirect">Libyan Civil War</a>. Initially developing his own variant of <a href="/wiki/Arab_nationalism" title="Arab nationalism">Arab nationalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arab_socialism" title="Arab socialism">Arab socialism</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Third_International_Theory" title="Third International Theory">Third International Theory</a>, he later embraced <a href="/wiki/Pan-Africanism" title="Pan-Africanism">Pan-Africanism</a> and served as <a href="/wiki/Chairperson_of_the_African_Union" title="Chairperson of the African Union">Chairperson</a> of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> from 2009 to 2010.</p>
<p>The son of an impoverished <a href="/wiki/Bedouin" title="Bedouin">Bedouin</a> goat herder, Gaddafi became involved in politics while at school in <a href="/wiki/Sabha,_Libya" title="Sabha, Libya">Sabha</a>, subsequently enrolling in the <a href="/wiki/Benghazi_Military_University_Academy" title="Benghazi Military University Academy">Royal Military Academy, Benghazi</a>. Founding a revolutionary cell within the military, in 1969 they seized power from the <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a> of <a href="/wiki/Idris_of_Libya" title="Idris of Libya">King Idris</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Nonviolent_revolution" title="Nonviolent revolution">bloodless</a> <a href="/wiki/Libyan_coup_d%27etat_(1969)" title="Libyan coup d'etat (1969)" class="mw-redirect">coup</a>. Becoming Chairman of the governing <a href="/wiki/Libyan_Revolutionary_Command_Council" title="Libyan Revolutionary Command Council">Revolutionary Command Council</a> (RCC), Gaddafi abolished the monarchy and proclaimed the Republic. <a href="/wiki/Rule_by_decree" title="Rule by decree">Ruling by decree</a>, he implemented measures to remove what he viewed as foreign <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">imperialist</a> influence from Libya, and strengthened ties to Arab nationalist governments. Intent on pushing Libya towards "<a href="/wiki/Islamic_socialism" title="Islamic socialism">Islamic socialism</a>", he introduced <i><a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">sharia</a></i> as the basis for the legal system and nationalized the oil industry, using the increased revenues to bolster the military, implement social programs and fund revolutionary militants across the world. In 1973 he initiated a "Popular Revolution" with the formation of <a href="/wiki/General_People%27s_Committee" title="General People's Committee">General People's Committees</a> (GPCs), purported to be a system of <a href="/wiki/Direct_democracy" title="Direct democracy">direct democracy</a>, but retained personal control over major decisions. He outlined his Third International Theory that year, publishing these ideas in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Green_Book_(Libya)" title="The Green Book (Libya)" class="mw-redirect">The Green Book</a></i>.</p>
<p>In 1977, Gaddafi dissolved the Republic and created a new <a href="/wiki/Socialist_state" title="Socialist state">socialist state</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Jamahiriya" title="Jamahiriya" class="mw-redirect">Jamahiriya</a></i> ("state of the masses"). Officially adopting a symbolic role in governance, he retained power as military commander-in-chief and head of the Revolutionary Committees responsible for policing and suppressing opponents. Overseeing unsuccessful border conflicts with Egypt and Chad, Gaddafi's support for foreign militants and alleged responsibility for the <a href="/wiki/Pan_Am_Flight_103" title="Pan Am Flight 103">Lockerbie bombing</a> led to Libya's label of "international pariah". A particularly hostile relationship developed with the United States and United Kingdom, resulting in the <a href="/wiki/1986_United_States_bombing_of_Libya" title="1986 United States bombing of Libya">1986 U.S. bombing of Libya</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>-imposed economic sanctions. Rejecting his earlier ideological commitments, from 1999 Gaddafi encouraged economic privatization and sought rapprochement with Western nations, also embracing Pan-Africanism and helping to establish the African Union. Amid the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a>, in 2011 an anti-Gaddafist uprising led by the <a href="/wiki/National_Transitional_Council" title="National Transitional Council">National Transitional Council</a> (NTC) broke out, resulting in civil war. <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> <a href="/wiki/2011_military_intervention_in_Libya" title="2011 military intervention in Libya">intervened militarily</a> on the side of the NTC, bringing about the government's downfall. Retreating to <a href="/wiki/Sirte" title="Sirte">Sirte</a>, Gaddafi was <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Muammar_Gaddafi" title="Death of Muammar Gaddafi">captured and killed</a> by NTC militants.</p>
<p>Gaddafi was a controversial and highly divisive world figure. Supporters lauded his <a href="/wiki/Anti-imperialism" title="Anti-imperialism">anti-imperialist</a> stance and his support for Pan-Africanism and <a href="/wiki/Pan-Arabism" title="Pan-Arabism">Pan-Arabism</a>, and he was decorated with various awards. Conversely, he was internationally condemned as a dictator and autocrat whose authoritarian administration violated the <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Libya" title="Human rights in Libya">human rights of Libyan citizens</a>, and supported irredentist movements, tribal warfare and <a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">terrorism</a> in many other nations.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Childhood:_1942.2F43.E2.80.9350">Childhood: 1942/43–50</span></h3>
<p>Muammar Gaddafi was born in a tent near <a href="/wiki/Qasr_Abu_Hadi" title="Qasr Abu Hadi">Qasr Abu Hadi</a>, a rural area outside the town of <a href="/wiki/Sirte" title="Sirte">Sirte</a> in the deserts of western Libya.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198733Kawczynski20119Bruce_St._John2012135_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198733Kawczynski20119Bruce_St._John2012135-15"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> His family came from a small, relatively un-influential tribal group called the <a href="/wiki/Qadhadhfa" title="Qadhadhfa">Qadhadhfa</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198733Kawczynski20119_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198733Kawczynski20119-16"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> who were <a href="/wiki/Arabized_Berber" title="Arabized Berber">Arabized Berber</a> in heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198645_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198645-17"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> His father, Mohammad Abdul Salam bin Hamed bin Mohammad, was known as Abu Meniar (died 1985), and his mother was named Aisha (died 1978); Abu Meniar earned a meager subsistence as a goat and camel herder.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198733Kawczynski20119_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198733Kawczynski20119-16"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Nomadic <a href="/wiki/Bedouin" title="Bedouin">Bedouins</a>, they were illiterate and kept no birth records.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198735Kawczynski20119Bruce_St._John2012135_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198735Kawczynski20119Bruce_St._John2012135-18"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> As such, Gaddafi's date of birth is not known with certainty, and sources have set it in 1942 or in the spring of 1943, although biographers Blundy and Lycett noted that it could have been pre-1940.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198735Kawczynski20119Bruce_St._John2012135_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198735Kawczynski20119Bruce_St._John2012135-18"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> His parents' only surviving son, he had three older sisters.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198735Kawczynski20119Bruce_St._John2012135_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198735Kawczynski20119Bruce_St._John2012135-18"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> Gaddafi's upbringing in Bedouin culture influenced his personal tastes for the rest of his life. He repeatedly expressed a preference for the desert over the city and retreated to the desert to meditate.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKawczynski20119Bruce_St._John2012135_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKawczynski20119Bruce_St._John2012135-19"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>From childhood, Gaddafi was aware of the involvement of European colonialists in Libya; his nation was <a href="/wiki/Italian_Libya" title="Italian Libya">occupied by Italy</a>, and during the <a href="/wiki/North_African_Campaign" title="North African Campaign">North African Campaign</a> of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> it witnessed conflict between Italian and British troops.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198735.E2.80.9337Bruce_St._John2012135_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198735.E2.80.9337Bruce_St._John2012135-20"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> According to later claims, Gaddafi's paternal grandfather, Abdessalam Bouminyar, was killed by the Italian Army during the <a href="/wiki/Italo-Turkish_War" title="Italo-Turkish War">Italian invasion of 1911</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBianco19754BlundyLycett198737Kawczynski20114_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBianco19754BlundyLycett198737Kawczynski20114-21"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> At World War II's end in 1945, Libya was occupied by British and French forces. Although Britain and France intended on dividing the nation between their empires, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">General Assembly of the United Nations</a> (UN) declared that the country be granted political independence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198738.E2.80.9339Kawczynski20117.E2.80.939.2C_14Bruce_St._John2012108_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198738.E2.80.9339Kawczynski20117.E2.80.939.2C_14Bruce_St._John2012108-22"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1951, the UN created the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Libya" title="Kingdom of Libya">United Kingdom of Libya</a>, a federal state under the leadership of a pro-western monarch, <a href="/wiki/Idris_of_Libya" title="Idris of Libya">Idris</a>, who banned political parties and established an <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198738.E2.80.9339Kawczynski20117.E2.80.939.2C_14Bruce_St._John2012108_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198738.E2.80.9339Kawczynski20117.E2.80.939.2C_14Bruce_St._John2012108-22"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_political_activism:_1950.E2.80.9363">Education and political activism: 1950–63</span></h3>
<p>Gaddafi's earliest education was of a religious nature, imparted by a local Islamic teacher.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBianco19755Bruce_St._John2012135.E2.80.93136_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBianco19755Bruce_St._John2012135.E2.80.93136-23"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Subsequently moving to nearby Sirte to attend elementary school, he progressed through six grades in four years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBianco19755.E2.80.936.2C_8.E2.80.939BlundyLycett198739Kawczynski201110Bruce_St._John2012136_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBianco19755.E2.80.936.2C_8.E2.80.939BlundyLycett198739Kawczynski201110Bruce_St._John2012136-24"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Education in Libya was not free, but his father thought it would greatly benefit his son despite the financial strain. During the week Gaddafi slept in a <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosque</a>, and at weekends walked 20 miles to visit his parents. Bullied for being a Bedouin, he was proud of his identity and encouraged pride in other Bedouin children.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBianco19755.E2.80.936.2C_8.E2.80.939BlundyLycett198739Kawczynski201110Bruce_St._John2012136_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBianco19755.E2.80.936.2C_8.E2.80.939BlundyLycett198739Kawczynski201110Bruce_St._John2012136-24"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> From Sirte, he and his family moved to the market town of <a href="/wiki/Sabha,_Libya" title="Sabha, Libya">Sabha</a> in <a href="/wiki/Fezzan" title="Fezzan">Fezzan</a>, south-central Libya, where his father worked as a caretaker for a tribal leader while Muammar attended secondary school, something neither parent had done.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198739Kawczynski201110.E2.80.9311Bruce_St._John2012136_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198739Kawczynski201110.E2.80.9311Bruce_St._John2012136-25"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Gaddafi was popular at school; some friends made there received significant jobs in his later administration, most notably his best friend <a href="/wiki/Abdessalam_Jalloud" title="Abdessalam Jalloud">Abdul Salam Jalloud</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198739.E2.80.9340Kawczynski201111_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198739.E2.80.9340Kawczynski201111-26"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nasser_portrait2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Nasser_portrait2.jpg/150px-Nasser_portrait2.jpg" width="150" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Nasser_portrait2.jpg/225px-Nasser_portrait2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Nasser_portrait2.jpg/300px-Nasser_portrait2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="424" data-file-height="500" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nasser_portrait2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Egyptian <a href="/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser" title="Gamal Abdel Nasser">President Nasser</a> was Gaddafi's schoolboy hero.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Many teachers at Sabha were Egyptian, and for the first time Gaddafi had access to pan-Arab newspapers and radio broadcasts, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>-based <i><a href="/wiki/Voice_of_the_Arabs" title="Voice of the Arabs">Voice of the Arabs</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198740Kawczynski201111.E2.80.9312Bruce_St._John2012136_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198740Kawczynski201111.E2.80.9312Bruce_St._John2012136-27"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> Growing up, Gaddafi witnessed significant events rock the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/1948_Arab-Israeli_War" title="1948 Arab-Israeli War" class="mw-redirect">1948 Arab-Israeli War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Revolution_of_1952" title="Egyptian Revolution of 1952">Egyptian Revolution of 1952</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Crisis" title="Suez Crisis">Suez Crisis</a> of 1956, and the short-lived existence of the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Republic" title="United Arab Republic">United Arab Republic</a> between 1958 and 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012136_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012136-28"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> Gaddafi admired the political changes implemented in the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Republic_of_Egypt" title="Arab Republic of Egypt" class="mw-redirect">Arab Republic of Egypt</a> under his hero, President <a href="/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser" title="Gamal Abdel Nasser">Gamal Abdel Nasser</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198740Vandewalle200810Kawczynski201111.E2.80.9312Bruce_St._John2012136_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198740Vandewalle200810Kawczynski201111.E2.80.9312Bruce_St._John2012136-29"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Nasser argued for <a href="/wiki/Arab_nationalism" title="Arab nationalism">Arab nationalism</a>; the rejection of Western <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonialism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neo-colonialism" title="Neo-colonialism" class="mw-redirect">neo-colonialism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zionism" title="Zionism">zionism</a>; and a transition from <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalism</a> to <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialism</a>. Nasser's book, <i>Philosophy of the Revolution</i>, was a key influence on Gaddafi; outlining how to initiate a coup, it has been described as "the inspiration and blueprint of [Gaddafi's] revolution."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198740Vandewalle200810Kawczynski201111.E2.80.9312Bruce_St._John2012136_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198740Vandewalle200810Kawczynski201111.E2.80.9312Bruce_St._John2012136-29"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Gaddafi organized demonstrations and distributed posters criticizing the monarchy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198742.E2.80.9343Kawczynski201111.E2.80.9312Bruce_St._John2012136_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198742.E2.80.9343Kawczynski201111.E2.80.9312Bruce_St._John2012136-30"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> In October 1961, he led a demonstration protesting Syria's secession from the United Arab Republic. During this they broke windows of a local hotel accused of serving alcohol. Catching the authorities' attention, they expelled his family from Sabha.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198742.E2.80.9343Kawczynski201111Bruce_St._John2012136_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198742.E2.80.9343Kawczynski201111Bruce_St._John2012136-31"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> Gaddafi moved to <a href="/wiki/Misrata" title="Misrata">Misrata</a>, there attending Misrata Secondary School.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198744Kawczynski201111Bruce_St._John2012137_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198744Kawczynski201111Bruce_St._John2012137-32"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> Maintaining his interest in Arab nationalist activism, he refused to join any of the banned political parties active in the city – including the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Nationalist_Movement" title="Arab Nationalist Movement">Arab Nationalist Movement</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Libyan_Arab_Socialist_Ba%27ath_Party" title="Libyan Arab Socialist Ba'ath Party" class="mw-redirect">Arab Socialist Ba'ath Party</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Brotherhood" title="Muslim Brotherhood">Muslim Brotherhood</a> – claiming he rejected factionalism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012137_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012137-33"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> He read voraciously on the subjects of Nasser and the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution_of_1789" title="French Revolution of 1789" class="mw-redirect">French Revolution of 1789</a>, as well as the works of Syrian political theorist <a href="/wiki/Michel_Aflaq" title="Michel Aflaq">Michel Aflaq</a> and biographies of <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen" title="Sun Yat-sen">Sun Yat-sen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk" title="Mustafa Kemal Atatürk">Mustafa Kemal Atatürk</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012137_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012137-33"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_training:_1963.E2.80.9366">Military training: 1963–66</span></h3>
<p>Gaddafi briefly studied History at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Libya" title="University of Libya">University of Libya</a> in <a href="/wiki/Benghazi" title="Benghazi">Benghazi</a>, before dropping out to join the military.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198646.E2.80.9347Bruce_St._John2012138_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198646.E2.80.9347Bruce_St._John2012138-34"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite his police record, in 1963 he began training at the <a href="/wiki/Benghazi_Military_University_Academy" title="Benghazi Military University Academy">Royal Military Academy</a>, Benghazi, alongside several like-minded friends from Misrata. The armed forces offered the only opportunity for upward social mobility for underprivileged Libyans, and Gaddafi recognised it as a potential instrument of political change.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198745Kawczynski201112Bruce_St._John2012138_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198745Kawczynski201112Bruce_St._John2012138-35"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> Under Idris, Libya's armed forces were trained by the British military; this angered Gaddafi, who viewed the British as imperialists, and accordingly he refused to learn English and was rude to the British officers, ultimately failing his exams.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198745_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198745-36"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> British trainers reported him for insubordination and abusive behaviour, stating their suspicion that he was involved in the assassination of the military academy's commander in 1963. Such reports were ignored and Gaddafi quickly progressed through the course.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198746.2C_48.E2.80.9349_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198746.2C_48.E2.80.9349-37"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gaddafi_in_London.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e2/Gaddafi_in_London.jpg/250px-Gaddafi_in_London.jpg" width="250" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e2/Gaddafi_in_London.jpg/375px-Gaddafi_in_London.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/e/e2/Gaddafi_in_London.jpg 2x" data-file-width="425" data-file-height="300" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gaddafi_in_London.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gaddafi in <a href="/wiki/Piccadilly" title="Piccadilly">Piccadilly</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, 1966.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With a group of loyal cadres, in 1964 Gaddafi founded the Central Committee of the Free Officers Movement, a revolutionary group named after Nasser's <a href="/wiki/Free_Officers_Movement_(Egypt)" title="Free Officers Movement (Egypt)">Egyptian predecessor</a>. Led by Gaddafi, they met clandestinely and were organised into a <a href="/wiki/Clandestine_cell_system" title="Clandestine cell system">clandestine cell system</a>, offering their salaries into a single fund.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198747.E2.80.9348Kawczynski201112.E2.80.9313_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198747.E2.80.9348Kawczynski201112.E2.80.9313-38"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Gaddafi travelled around Libya gathering intelligence and developing connections with sympathisers, but the government's intelligence services ignored him, considering him little threat.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201113_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201113-39"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Graduating in August 1965,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012138_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012138-40"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> Gaddafi became a communications officer in the army's signal corps.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012138_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012138-40"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> In April 1966, he was assigned to the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> for further training; over 9 months he underwent an English-language course at <a href="/wiki/Beaconsfield" title="Beaconsfield">Beaconsfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buckinghamshire" title="Buckinghamshire">Buckinghamshire</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Army_Air_Corps_(United_Kingdom)" title="Army Air Corps (United Kingdom)">Army Air Corps</a> signal instructors course in <a href="/wiki/Bovington_Camp" title="Bovington Camp">Bovington Camp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dorset" title="Dorset">Dorset</a>, and an infantry signal instructors course at <a href="/wiki/Hythe,_Kent" title="Hythe, Kent">Hythe, Kent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198749.E2.80.9350Kawczynski201113Bruce_St._John2012138_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198749.E2.80.9350Kawczynski201113Bruce_St._John2012138-41"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite later rumours to the contrary, he did not attend the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Military_Academy_Sandhurst" title="Royal Military Academy Sandhurst">Royal Military Academy Sandhurst</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201113_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201113-39"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Bovington signal course's director reported that Gaddafi successfully overcame problems learning English, displaying a firm command of voice procedure. Noting that Gaddafi's favourite hobbies were reading and playing <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, he thought him an "amusing officer, always cheerful, hard-working, and conscientious."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012138.E2.80.93139_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012138.E2.80.93139-42"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> Gaddafi disliked England, claiming British Army officers racially insulted him and finding it difficult adjusting to the country's culture; asserting his Arab identity in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, he walked around <a href="/wiki/Piccadilly" title="Piccadilly">Piccadilly</a> wearing traditional Libyan robes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198749.E2.80.9350Kawczynski201113Bruce_St._John2012139_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198749.E2.80.9350Kawczynski201113Bruce_St._John2012139-43"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> He later related that while he travelled to England believing it more advanced than Libya, he returned home "more confident and proud of our values, ideals and social character."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198749.E2.80.9350Kawczynski201113Bruce_St._John2012139_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198749.E2.80.9350Kawczynski201113Bruce_St._John2012139-43"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Libyan_Arab_Republic">Libyan Arab Republic</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Libya_under_Muammar_Gaddafi" title="History of Libya under Muammar Gaddafi">History of Libya under Muammar Gaddafi</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coup_d.27etat:_1969">Coup d'etat: 1969</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1969_Libyan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1969 Libyan coup d'état">1969 Libyan coup d'état</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nasser_Qaddafi_Atassi_1969.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Nasser_Qaddafi_Atassi_1969.jpg/300px-Nasser_Qaddafi_Atassi_1969.jpg" width="300" height="234" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Nasser_Qaddafi_Atassi_1969.jpg/450px-Nasser_Qaddafi_Atassi_1969.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Nasser_Qaddafi_Atassi_1969.jpg/600px-Nasser_Qaddafi_Atassi_1969.jpg 2x" data-file-width="709" data-file-height="552" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nasser_Qaddafi_Atassi_1969.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gaddafi at an Arab summit in Libya in 1969, shortly after the September Revolution that toppled <a href="/wiki/King_Idris_I" title="King Idris I" class="mw-redirect">King Idris I</a>. Gaddafi sits in military uniform in the middle, surrounded by President <a href="/wiki/Gamal_Abd_al-Nasser" title="Gamal Abd al-Nasser" class="mw-redirect">Gamal Abd al-Nasser</a> (left) and Syrian President <a href="/wiki/Nur_al-Din_al-Atasi" title="Nur al-Din al-Atasi" class="mw-redirect">Nur al-Din al-Atasi</a> (right).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Idris' government was increasingly unpopular by the latter 1960s; it had exacerbated Libya's traditional regional and tribal divisions by <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">centralising</a> the country's <a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">federal system</a> in order to take advantage of the country's oil wealth,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198614BlundyLycett198752Kawczynski201115.E2.80.9316_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198614BlundyLycett198752Kawczynski201115.E2.80.9316-44"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> while corruption and entrenched systems of patronage were widespread throughout the oil industry.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198751Kawczynski2011136_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198751Kawczynski2011136-45"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Arab nationalism was increasingly popular, and protests flared up following Egypt's 1967 defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Six-Day_War" title="Six-Day War">Six-Day War</a> with Israel; allied to the western powers, Idris' administration was seen as pro-Israeli.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201116.E2.80.9317_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201116.E2.80.9317-46"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> Anti-western riots broke out in Tripoli and Benghazi, while Libyan workers shut down oil terminals in solidarity with Egypt.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201116.E2.80.9317_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201116.E2.80.9317-46"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> By 1969, the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a> was expecting segments of Libya's armed forces to launch a coup. Although claims have been made that they knew of Gaddafi's Free Officers Movement, they have since claimed ignorance, stating that they were monitoring Abdul Aziz Shalhi's Black Boots revolutionary group.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198753Kawczynski201119Bruce_St._John2012139.E2.80.93140_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198753Kawczynski201119Bruce_St._John2012139.E2.80.93140-47"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In mid-1969, Idris travelled abroad to spend the summer in Turkey and Greece. Gaddafi's Free Officers recognized this as their chance to overthrow the monarchy, initiating "Operation Jerusalem".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201118_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201118-48"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> On 1 September, they occupied airports, police depots, radio stations and government offices in Tripoli and Benghazi. Gaddafi took control of the Berka barracks in Benghazi, while <a href="/w/index.php?title=Omar_Meheisha&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Omar Meheisha (page does not exist)">Omar Meheisha</a> occupied Tripoli barracks and Jalloud seized the city's anti-aircraft batteries. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Khweldi_Hameidi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Khweldi Hameidi (page does not exist)">Khweldi Hameidi</a> was sent to arrest crown prince <a href="/wiki/Hasan_as-Senussi" title="Hasan as-Senussi">Sayyid Hasan ar-Rida al-Mahdi as-Sanussi</a>, and force him to relinquish his claim to the throne.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198614BlundyLycett198757.E2.80.9359Kawczynski201118_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198614BlundyLycett198757.E2.80.9359Kawczynski201118-49"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> They met no serious resistance, and wielded little violence against the monarchists.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201118_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201118-48"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Having removed the monarchical government, Gaddafi proclaimed the foundation of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Libya_under_Muammar_Gaddafi" title="History of Libya under Muammar Gaddafi">Libyan Arab Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198615_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198615-50"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> Addressing the populace by radio, he proclaimed an end to the "reactionary and corrupt" regime, "the stench of which has sickened and horrified us all."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198614BlundyLycett198759.E2.80.9360Kawczynski201118_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198614BlundyLycett198759.E2.80.9360Kawczynski201118-51"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Due to the coup's bloodless nature, it was initially labelled the "White Revolution", although was later renamed the "One September Revolution" after the date on which it occurred.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012134_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012134-52"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> Gaddafi insisted that the Free Officers' coup represented a revolution, marking the start of widespread change in the socio-economic and political nature of Libya.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012159_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012159-53"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> He proclaimed that the revolution meant "freedom, <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialism</a>, and unity", and over the coming years implemented measures to achieve this.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198615BlundyLycett198764Bruce_St._John2012148_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198615BlundyLycett198764Bruce_St._John2012148-54"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consolidating_leadership:_1969.E2.80.9373">Consolidating leadership: 1969–73</span></h3>
<p>The 12 member central committee of the Free Officers proclaimed themselves the <a href="/wiki/Libyan_Revolutionary_Command_Council" title="Libyan Revolutionary Command Council">Revolutionary Command Council</a> (RCC), the government of the new republic.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198763Vandewalle20089Bruce_St._John2012134_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198763Vandewalle20089Bruce_St._John2012134-55"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> Gaddafi became RCC Chairman, and therefore the <i>de facto</i> head of state, also appointing himself to the rank of Colonel and becoming commander-in-chief of the armed forces.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198615BlundyLycett198764Bruce_St._John2012134_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198615BlundyLycett198764Bruce_St._John2012134-56"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> Jalloud became Prime Minister,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198791.E2.80.9392_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198791.E2.80.9392-57"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> while a civilian Council of Ministers headed by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sulaiman_Maghribi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sulaiman Maghribi (page does not exist)">Sulaiman Maghribi</a> was founded to implement RCC policy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198617BlundyLycett198763_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198617BlundyLycett198763-58"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Libya_(1969%E2%80%931972).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Flag_of_Libya_%281969%E2%80%931972%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_Libya_%281969%E2%80%931972%29.svg.png" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Flag_of_Libya_%281969%E2%80%931972%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_Libya_%281969%E2%80%931972%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Flag_of_Libya_%281969%E2%80%931972%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_Libya_%281969%E2%80%931972%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Libya_(1969%E2%80%931972).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Libya" title="Flag of Libya">Flag</a> of the Libyan Arab Republic (1969–1977)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although theoretically a collegial body operating through consensus building, Gaddafi dominated the RCC,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012134_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012134-52"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> although some of the others attempted to constrain what they saw as his excesses.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201120_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201120-59"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> Gaddafi remained the government's public face, with the identities of the other RCC members only being publicly revealed on 10 January 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVandewalle20089Bruce_St._John2012134_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVandewalle20089Bruce_St._John2012134-60"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> All young men from (typically rural) working and middle-class backgrounds, none had university degrees; in this way they were distinct from the wealthy, highly educated conservatives who previously governed the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198638Vandewalle200810Kawczynski201120_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198638Vandewalle200810Kawczynski201120-61"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The coup completed, the RCC proceeded with their intentions of consolidating the revolutionary government and modernizing the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012134_52-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012134-52"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> They purged monarchists and members of Idris' <a href="/wiki/Senussi" title="Senussi">Senussi</a> clan from Libya's political world and armed forces; Gaddafi believed this elite were opposed to the will of the Libyan people and had to be expunged.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVandewalle200811Kawczynski201121.E2.80.9323_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVandewalle200811Kawczynski201121.E2.80.9323-62"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> "People's Courts" were founded to try various monarchist politicians and journalists, and though many were imprisoned, none were executed. Idris was sentenced to execution <i>in absentia</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198616BlundyLycett198762_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198616BlundyLycett198762-63"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In May 1970, the Revolutionary Intellectuals Seminar was held to bring intellectuals in line with the revolution,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198617_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198617-64"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> while that year's Legislative Review and Amendment united secular and religious law codes, introducing <i><a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">sharia</a></i> into the legal system.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198616_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198616-65"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rule_by_decree" title="Rule by decree">Ruling by decree</a>, the RCC maintained the monarchy's ban on political parties, in May 1970 banned <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">trade unions</a>, and in 1972 outlawed workers' strikes and suspended newspapers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198617BlundyLycett198763.E2.80.9364Vandewalle200811Bruce_St._John2012153_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198617BlundyLycett198763.E2.80.9364Vandewalle200811Bruce_St._John2012153-66"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 1971, Gaddafi resigned, claiming to be dissatisfied with the pace of reform, but returned to his position within a month.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198791.E2.80.9392_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198791.E2.80.9392-57"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> In February 1973, he resigned again, once more returning the following month.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198785_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198785-67"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_and_social_reform">Economic and social reform</span></h4>
<p>With <a href="/wiki/Crude_oil" title="Crude oil" class="mw-redirect">crude oil</a> as the country's primary export, Gaddafi sought to improve Libya's oil sector.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198766.E2.80.9367Bruce_St._John2012145.E2.80.93146_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198766.E2.80.9367Bruce_St._John2012145.E2.80.93146-68"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> In October 1969, he proclaimed the current trade terms unfair, benefiting foreign corporations more than the Libyan state, and by threatening to reduce production, in December Jalloud successfully increased the price of Libyan oil.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198766.E2.80.9367Bruce_St._John2012145.E2.80.93146_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198766.E2.80.9367Bruce_St._John2012145.E2.80.93146-68"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1970, other <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a> states followed suit, leading to a global increase in the price of crude oil.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198766.E2.80.9367Bruce_St._John2012145.E2.80.93146_68-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198766.E2.80.9367Bruce_St._John2012145.E2.80.93146-68"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> The RCC followed with the Tripoli Agreement, in which they secured income tax, back-payments and better pricing from the oil corporations; these measures brought Libya an estimated $1 billion in additional revenues in its first year.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVandewalle200815Bruce_St._John2012147_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVandewalle200815Bruce_St._John2012147-69"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Increasing state control over the oil sector, the RCC began a program of <a href="/wiki/Nationalization" title="Nationalization">nationalization</a>, starting with the expropriation of <a href="/wiki/British_Petroleum" title="British Petroleum" class="mw-redirect">British Petroleum</a>'s share of the British Petroleum-N.B. Hunt Sahir Field in December 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198768Bruce_St._John2012147_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198768Bruce_St._John2012147-70"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 1973, it was announced that all foreign oil producers active in Libya were to be nationalized. For Gaddafi, this was an important step towards socialism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198768Bruce_St._John2012147_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198768Bruce_St._John2012147-70"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> It proved an economic success; while gross domestic product had been $3.8 billion in 1969, it had risen to $13.7 billion in 1974, and $24.5 billion in 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett1987107_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett1987107-71"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> In turn, the Libyans' standard of life greatly improved over the first decade of Gaddafi's administration, and by 1979 the average per-capita income was at $8,170, up from $40 in 1951; this was above the average of many industrialized countries like Italy and the U.K.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett1987107_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett1987107-71"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sadat_Qaddafi_Assad_1971.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Sadat_Qaddafi_Assad_1971.jpg/250px-Sadat_Qaddafi_Assad_1971.jpg" width="250" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Sadat_Qaddafi_Assad_1971.jpg/375px-Sadat_Qaddafi_Assad_1971.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Sadat_Qaddafi_Assad_1971.jpg/500px-Sadat_Qaddafi_Assad_1971.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="426" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sadat_Qaddafi_Assad_1971.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
In 1971, Egypt's <a href="/wiki/Anwar_Sadat" title="Anwar Sadat">Anwar Sadat</a>, Libya's Gaddafi and Syria's <a href="/wiki/Hafez_al-Assad" title="Hafez al-Assad">Hafez al-Assad</a> signed an agreement <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Arab_Republics" title="Federation of Arab Republics">to form a federal Union of Arab Republics</a>. The agreement never materialized into a federal union between the three Arab states.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The RCC attempted to suppress regional and tribal affiliation, replacing it with a unified pan-Libyan identity.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012154_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012154-72"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> In doing so, they tried discrediting tribal leaders as agents of the old regime, and in August 1971 a Sabha military court tried many of them for counter-revolutionary activity.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012154_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012154-72"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> Long-standing administrative boundaries were re-drawn, crossing tribal boundaries, while pro-revolutionary modernizers replaced traditional leaders, but the communities they served often rejected them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012154.E2.80.93155_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012154.E2.80.93155-73"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> Realizing the failures of the modernizers, Gaddafi created the <a href="/wiki/Libyan_Arab_Socialist_Union" title="Libyan Arab Socialist Union">Arab Socialist Union</a> (ASU), a mass mobilization <a href="/wiki/Vanguard_party" title="Vanguard party" class="mw-redirect">vanguard party</a> of which he was president.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198791Vandewalle200811Bruce_St._John2012155_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198791Vandewalle200811Bruce_St._John2012155-74"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> The ASU recognized the RCC as its "Supreme Leading Authority", and was designed to further revolutionary enthusiasm throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198791Vandewalle200811Bruce_St._John2012155_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198791Vandewalle200811Bruce_St._John2012155-74"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The RCC implemented measures for social reform, adopting <i>sharia</i> as a basis.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198764Vandewalle200831Kawczynski201121Bruce_St._John2012134_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198764Vandewalle200831Kawczynski201121Bruce_St._John2012134-75"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> The consumption of alcohol was banned, night clubs and Christian churches were shut down, traditional Libyan dress was encouraged, while Arabic was decreed as the only language permitted in official communications and on road signs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198764Vandewalle200831Kawczynski201121Bruce_St._John2012134_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198764Vandewalle200831Kawczynski201121Bruce_St._John2012134-75"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> From 1969 to 1973, the RCC introduced social welfare programs funded with oil money, which led to house-building projects and improved healthcare and education.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201123Bruce_St._John2012149_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201123Bruce_St._John2012149-76"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> In doing so, they greatly expanded the <a href="/wiki/Public_sector" title="Public sector">public sector</a>, providing employment for thousands.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201123Bruce_St._John2012149_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201123Bruce_St._John2012149-76"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Compulsory education was expanded from 6 to 9 years old, while adult literacy programs and free university education were implemented; <a href="/wiki/Beida_University" title="Beida University" class="mw-redirect">Beida University</a> was founded, while <a href="/wiki/Tripoli_University" title="Tripoli University" class="mw-redirect">Tripoli University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Benghazi_University" title="Benghazi University" class="mw-redirect">Benghazi University</a> were expanded.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198638_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198638-77"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> These early social programs proved popular within Libya.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198619Kawczynski201122Bruce_St._John2012149_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198619Kawczynski201122Bruce_St._John2012149-78"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> This popularity was partly due to Gaddafi's personal charisma, youth and underdog status as a Bedouin, as well as his rhetoric emphasizing his role as the successor to the anti-Italian fighter <a href="/wiki/Omar_Mukhtar" title="Omar Mukhtar">Omar Mukhtar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVandewalle200831.E2.80.9332Kawczynski201122_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVandewalle200831.E2.80.9332Kawczynski201122-79"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Libya_under_Muammar_Gaddafi" title="Foreign relations of Libya under Muammar Gaddafi">Foreign relations of Libya under Muammar Gaddafi</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nasser_Gaddafi_1969.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Nasser_Gaddafi_1969.jpg/200px-Nasser_Gaddafi_1969.jpg" width="200" height="249" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Nasser_Gaddafi_1969.jpg/300px-Nasser_Gaddafi_1969.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c1/Nasser_Gaddafi_1969.jpg 2x" data-file-width="321" data-file-height="400" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nasser_Gaddafi_1969.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gaddafi (left) with Egyptian President Nasser in 1969. Nasser privately thought Gaddafi "a nice boy, but terribly naive".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198718_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198718-80"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The influence of Nasser's Arab nationalism over the RCC was immediately apparent.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVandewalle20089Bruce_St._John2012137_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVandewalle20089Bruce_St._John2012137-81"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> The administration was instantly <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_recognition" title="Diplomatic recognition">recognized</a> by the neighbouring Arab nationalist regimes in Egypt, Syria, Iraq and Sudan,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198760Kawczynski201118_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198760Kawczynski201118-82"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> with Egypt sending experts to aid the inexperienced RCC.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198762.E2.80.9363Kawczynski201118_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198762.E2.80.9363Kawczynski201118-83"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> Gaddafi propounded <a href="/wiki/Pan-Arab" title="Pan-Arab" class="mw-redirect">Pan-Arab</a> ideas, proclaiming the need for a single Arab state stretching across North Africa and the Middle East. In December 1969, Libya founded the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Arab_Revolutionary_Front&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Arab Revolutionary Front (page does not exist)">Arab Revolutionary Front</a> with Egypt and Sudan as a step towards political unification, and in 1970 Syria stated its intention to join.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198775Kawczynski201165Bruce_St._John2012186_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198775Kawczynski201165Bruce_St._John2012186-84"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After Nasser died in November 1970, his successor, <a href="/wiki/Anwar_Sadat" title="Anwar Sadat">Anwar Sadat</a>, suggested that rather than a unified state, they create <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Arab_Republics" title="Federation of Arab Republics">a political federation</a>, implemented in April 1971; in doing so, Egypt, Syria and Sudan got large grants of Libyan oil money.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198687Kawczynski201165Bruce_St._John2012151.E2.80.93152_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198687Kawczynski201165Bruce_St._John2012151.E2.80.93152-85"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> In February 1972, Gaddafi and Sadat signed an unofficial charter of merger, but it was never implemented as relations broke down the following year. Sadat became increasingly wary of Libya's radical direction, and the September 1973 deadline for implementing the Federation passed by with no action taken.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201166Bruce_St._John2012182_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201166Bruce_St._John2012182-86"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After the 1969 coup, representatives of the <a href="/wiki/Allied_Control_Council" title="Allied Control Council">Four Powers</a> – France, the United Kingdom, the United States and the Soviet Union – were called to meet RCC representatives.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012140_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012140-87"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> The U.K. and U.S. quickly extended diplomatic recognition, hoping to secure the position of their military bases in Libya and fearing further instability. Hoping to ingratiate themselves with Gaddafi, in 1970 the U.S. informed him of at least one planned counter-coup.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198765Kawczynski201118Bruce_St._John2012140.E2.80.93141_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198765Kawczynski201118Bruce_St._John2012140.E2.80.93141-88"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> Such attempts to form a working relationship with the RCC failed; Gaddafi was determined to reassert national sovereignty and expunge what he described as foreign colonial and imperialist influences. His administration insisted that the U.S. and U.K. remove their military bases from Libya, with Gaddafi proclaiming that "the armed forces which rose to express the people's revolution [will not] tolerate living in their shacks while the bases of imperialism exist in Libyan territory." The British left in March and the Americans in June 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198761Kawczynski201119Bruce_St._John2012141.E2.80.93143_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198761Kawczynski201119Bruce_St._John2012141.E2.80.93143-89"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Moving to reduce Italian influence, in October 1970 all Italian-owned assets were expropriated and the 12,000-strong <a href="/wiki/Italian_settlers_in_Libya" title="Italian settlers in Libya">Italian community</a> expelled from Libya alongside a smaller number of Jews. The day became a <a href="/wiki/Public_holiday" title="Public holiday">national holiday</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198764Kawczynski201121.E2.80.9322Bruce_St._John2012142_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198764Kawczynski201121.E2.80.9322Bruce_St._John2012142-90"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> Aiming to reduce <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">North Atlantic Treaty Organization</a> (NATO) power in the Mediterranean, in 1971 Libya requested that Malta cease to allow NATO to use its land for a military base, in turn offering them foreign aid. Compromising, Malta's government continued allowing NATO use of the island, but only on the condition that they would not use it for launching attacks on Arab territory.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012150.E2.80.93151_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012150.E2.80.93151-91"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> Orchestrating a military build-up, the RCC began purchasing weapons from France and the Soviet Union. The commercial relationship with the latter led to an increasingly strained relationship with the U.S., who were then engaged in the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> with the Soviets.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012144.E2.80.93145_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012144.E2.80.93145-92"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
<div id="mwe_player_0" class="PopUpMediaTransform" style="width:250px;" videopayload="&lt;div class=&quot;mediaContainer&quot; style=&quot;position:relative;display:block;width:400px&quot;&gt;&lt;video id=&quot;mwe_player_1&quot; <div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oil_Rich_Libya.ogv" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A 1972 anti-Gaddafist British <a href="/wiki/Newsreel" title="Newsreel">newsreel</a> including an interview with Gaddafi about his support for foreign militants.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Gaddafi was especially critical of the U.S. due to their support for Israel. Gaddafi supported the <a href="/wiki/Palestinians" title="Palestinians">Palestinians</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian conflict" class="mw-redirect">Israeli-Palestinian conflict</a>, viewing the 1948 creation of Israel as a Western colonial occupation forced on the Arab world.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198770.E2.80.9371Vandewalle200834Kawczynski201164Bruce_St._John2012150.E2.80.93152_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198770.E2.80.9371Vandewalle200834Kawczynski201164Bruce_St._John2012150.E2.80.93152-93"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> Calling on the Arab states to wage "continuous war" against Israel, in 1970 he initiated a Jihad Fund to finance anti-Israeli militants.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198771Bruce_St._John2012185_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198771Bruce_St._John2012185-94"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 1972 Gaddafi created the First Nasserite Volunteers Centre to train anti-Israeli guerrillas.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201137Bruce_St._John2012151_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKawczynski201137Bruce_St._John2012151-95"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>His relationship with Palestinian leader <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a> of <a href="/wiki/Fatah" title="Fatah">Fatah</a> was strained, with Gaddafi considering him too moderate and calling for more violent action.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198769.E2.80.9370Kawczynski201137Bruce_St._John2012178_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198769.E2.80.9370Kawczynski201137Bruce_St._John2012178-96"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> Instead he supported militia like the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Front_for_the_Liberation_of_Palestine" title="Popular Front for the Liberation of Palestine">Popular Front for the Liberation of Palestine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Popular_Front_for_the_Liberation_of_Palestine_%E2%80%93_General_Command" title="Popular Front for the Liberation of Palestine – General Command">Popular Front for the Liberation of Palestine – General Command</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Front_for_the_Liberation_of_Palestine" title="Democratic Front for the Liberation of Palestine">Democratic Front for the Liberation of Palestine</a>, <a href="/wiki/As-Sa%27iqa" title="As-Sa'iqa">As-Sa'iqa</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Popular_Struggle_Front" title="Palestinian Popular Struggle Front">Palestinian Popular Struggle Front</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Abu_Nidal" title="Abu Nidal">Abu Nidal Organization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett1987150_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett1987150-97"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> He funded the <a href="/wiki/Black_September_(group)" title="Black September (group)" class="mw-redirect">Black September</a> group who perpetrated the 1972 <a href="/wiki/Munich_massacre" title="Munich massacre">Munich massacre</a> of Israeli athletes in West Germany, and had the killed militants' bodies flown to Libya for a hero's funeral.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198778Kawczynski201138Bruce_St._John2012178_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198778Kawczynski201138Bruce_St._John2012178-98"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Gaddafi also welcomed the three surviving attackers in Tripoli following their release in exchange for the hostages of hijacked <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Flight_615" title="Lufthansa Flight 615">Lufthansa Flight 615</a> a few weeks later and allowed them to go into hiding.<sup id="cite_ref-haaretz_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haaretz-99"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Gaddafi financially supported other militant groups across the world, including the <a href="/wiki/Black_Panther_Party" title="Black Panther Party">Black Panther Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nation_of_Islam" title="Nation of Islam">Nation of Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tupamaros" title="Tupamaros">Tupamaros</a>, <a href="/wiki/19th_of_April_Movement" title="19th of April Movement">19th of April Movement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sandinista_National_Liberation_Front" title="Sandinista National Liberation Front">Sandinista National Liberation Front</a> in the Americas, the <a href="/wiki/ANC" title="ANC" class="mw-redirect">ANC</a> among other <a href="/wiki/Liberation_movements" title="Liberation movements" class="mw-redirect">liberation movements</a> in the fight against <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">Apartheid</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> in Africa, the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Irish_Republican_Army" title="Provisional Irish Republican Army">Provisional Irish Republican Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/ETA_(separatist_group)" title="ETA (separatist group)">ETA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Action_directe_(armed_group)" title="Action directe (armed group)">Action directe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Red_Brigades" title="Red Brigades">Red Brigades</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army_Faction" title="Red Army Faction">Red Army Faction</a> in Europe, and the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Secret_Army_for_the_Liberation_of_Armenia" title="Armenian Secret Army for the Liberation of Armenia">Armenian Secret Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Red_Army" title="Japanese Red Army">Japanese Red Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Free_Aceh_Movement" title="Free Aceh Movement">Free Aceh Movement</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Moro_National_Liberation_Front" title="Moro National Liberation Front">Moro National Liberation Front</a> in Asia. Gaddafi was indiscriminate in the causes he funded, sometimes switching from supporting one side in a conflict to the other, as in the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_War_of_Independence" title="Eritrean War of Independence">Eritrean War of Independence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198778.E2.80.9381.2C_150.2C_185Kawczynski201134.E2.80.9335.2C_40.E2.80.9353Bruce_St._John2012151_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198778.E2.80.9381.2C_150.2C_185Kawczynski201134.E2.80.9335.2C_40.E2.80.9353Bruce_St._John2012151-100"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> Throughout the 1970s these groups received financial support from Libya, which came to be seen as a leader in the <a href="/wiki/Third_World" title="Third World">Third World</a>'s struggle against colonialism and neocolonialism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198778.E2.80.9381.2C_150Kawczynski201134.E2.80.9335.2C_40.E2.80.9353Bruce_St._John2012151_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198778.E2.80.9381.2C_150Kawczynski201134.E2.80.9335.2C_40.E2.80.9353Bruce_St._John2012151-101"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> Though many of these groups were labelled "<a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">terrorists</a>" by critics of their activities, Gaddafi rejected such a characterisation, instead considering them revolutionaries engaged in liberation struggles.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198655_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198655-102"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_.22Popular_Revolution.22:_1973.E2.80.9377">The "Popular Revolution": 1973–77</span></h3>
<p>On 16 April 1973, Gaddafi proclaimed the start of a "Popular Revolution" in a <a href="/wiki/Zuwara" title="Zuwara" class="mw-redirect">Zuwara</a> speech.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198785Vandewalle200812Kawczynski201122Bruce_St._John2012156_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198785Vandewalle200812Kawczynski201122Bruce_St._John2012156-103"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> He initiated this with a 5-point plan, the first point of which dissolved all existing laws, to be replaced by revolutionary enactments. The second point proclaimed that all opponents of the revolution had to be removed, while the third initiated an administrative revolution that Gaddafi proclaimed would remove all traces of <a href="/wiki/Bureaucracy" title="Bureaucracy">bureaucracy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bourgeoisie" title="Bourgeoisie">bourgeoisie</a>. The fourth point announced that the population must form People's Committees and be armed to defend the revolution, while the fifth proclaimed the beginning of a cultural revolution to expunge Libya of "poisonous" foreign influences.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198618BlundyLycett198785.E2.80.9386Kawczynski201122Bruce_St._John2012156_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198618BlundyLycett198785.E2.80.9386Kawczynski201122Bruce_St._John2012156-104"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> He began to lecture on this new phase of the revolution in Libya, Egypt, and France.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198793.E2.80.9394_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198793.E2.80.9394-105"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As part of this Popular Revolution, Gaddafi invited Libya's people to found <a href="/wiki/General_People%27s_Committee" title="General People's Committee">General People's Committees</a> as conduits for raising political consciousness. Although offering little guidance for how to set up these councils, Gaddafi claimed that they would offer a form of <a href="/wiki/Direct_democracy" title="Direct democracy">direct</a> <a href="/wiki/Participatory_democracy" title="Participatory democracy">political participation</a> that was more democratic than a traditional party-based <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative system</a>. He hoped that the councils would mobilize the people behind the RCC, erode the power of the traditional leaders and the bureaucracy, and allow for a new legal system chosen by the people.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198786Bruce_St._John2012156_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198786Bruce_St._John2012156-106"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The People's Committees led to a high percentage of public involvement in decision making, within the limits permitted by the RCC,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012157_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012157-107"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> but exacerbated tribal divisions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett1987103.E2.80.93104_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett1987103.E2.80.93104-108"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> They also served as a surveillance system, aiding the security services in locating individuals with views critical of the RCC, leading to the arrest of <a href="/wiki/Ba%27athism" title="Ba'athism">Ba'athists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islamism" title="Islamism">Islamists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198618BlundyLycett1987116Bruce_St._John2012157_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198618BlundyLycett1987116Bruce_St._John2012157-109"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> Operating in a pyramid structure, the base form of these Committees were local working groups, who sent elected representatives to the district level, and from there to the national level, divided between the <a href="/wiki/General_People%27s_Congress_(Libya)" title="General People's Congress (Libya)">General People's Congress</a> and the <a href="/wiki/General_People%27s_Committee" title="General People's Committee">General People's Committee</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett1987104Kawczynski201126_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett1987104Kawczynski201126-110"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Above these remained Gaddafi and the RCC, who remained responsible for all major decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198664Bruce_St._John2012163_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198664Bruce_St._John2012163-111"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Third_Universal_Theory_and_The_Green_Book">Third Universal Theory and <i>The Green Book</i></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Third_Universal_Theory" title="Third Universal Theory" class="mw-redirect">Third Universal Theory</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Green_Book_(Muammar_Gaddafi)" title="The Green Book (Muammar Gaddafi)">The Green Book (Muammar Gaddafi)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Green_book.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Green_book.jpg/250px-Green_book.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Green_book.jpg/375px-Green_book.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Green_book.jpg/500px-Green_book.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Green_book.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gaddafi's <a href="/wiki/The_Green_Book_(Muammar_Gaddafi)" title="The Green Book (Muammar Gaddafi)"><i>Green Book</i></a>. He informed an Italian journalist that "the Green Book is the guide to the emancipation of man. The Green Book is the gospel. The new gospel. The gospel of the new era, the era of the masses. In <a href="/wiki/Gospel" title="Gospel">your gospels</a> it's written: 'In the beginning there was the word.' The Green Book is the word. One of its words can destroy the world. Or save it. The Third World only needs my Green Book. My word."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198650_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198650-112"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In June 1973, Gaddafi created a political ideology as a basis for the Popular Revolution. <a href="/wiki/Third_Universal_Theory" title="Third Universal Theory" class="mw-redirect">Third Universal Theory</a> considered the U.S. and the Soviet Union as imperialist, thus rejected Western <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalism</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">Eastern bloc communism's</a> atheism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198786.E2.80.9387Bruce_St._John2012157.E2.80.93158_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett198786.E2.80.9387Bruce_St._John2012157.E2.80.93158-113"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> In this respect it was similar to the <a href="/wiki/Three_Worlds_Theory" title="Three Worlds Theory">Three Worlds Theory</a> developed by China's political leader <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198658_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198658-114"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> As part of this theory, Gaddafi praised <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalism</a> as a progressive force and advocated the creation of a pan-Arab state which would lead the Islamic and Third Worlds against imperialism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012158_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce_St._John2012158-115"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Gaddafi saw <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> as having a key role in this ideology, calling for an <a href="/wiki/Islamic_revival" title="Islamic revival">Islamic revival</a> that returned to the origins of the <a href="/wiki/Qur%27an" title="Qur'an" class="mw-redirect">Qur'an</a>, rejecting scholarly interpretations and the <a href="/wiki/Hadith" title="Hadith">Hadith</a>; in doing so, he angered many Libyan clerics.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris198649BlundyLycett1987122Bruce_St._John2012159_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris198649BlundyLycett1987122Bruce_St._John2012159-116"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> During 1973 and 1974, his government deepened the legal reliance on <i>sharia</i>, e.g. introducing flogging as punishment for those convicted of adultery or homosexual activity.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett1987112_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlundyLycett1987112-117"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Gaddafi summarized Third Universal Theory in three short volumes published between 1975 and 1979, collectively known as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Green_Book_(Muammar_Gaddafi)" title="The Green Book (Muammar Gaddafi)">The Green Book</a></i>. Volume one was devoted to the issue of democracy, outlining the flaws of representative systems in favour of direct, participatory GPCs. The second dealt with Gaddafi's beliefs regarding socialism, while the third explored social issues regarding the family and the tribe.
